\\n67:     <p>On compaction, we preserve the first and last offset/sequence numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\\n68:     producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, for example, then after a partition leader failure, the producer might see an OutOfSequence error. The base sequence number must\\n69:     be preserved for duplicate checking (the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer). As a result,\\n70:     it is possible to have empty batches in the log when all the records in the batch are cleaned but batch is still retained in order to preserve a producer's last sequence number. \\n67:     <p>On compaction, we preserve the first and last offset/sequence numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\\n68:     producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, for example, then after a partition leader failure, the producer might see an OutOfSequence error. The base sequence number must\\n69:     be preserved for duplicate checking (the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer). As a result,\\n70:     it is possible to have empty batches in the log when all the records in the batch are cleaned but batch is still retained in order to preserve a producer's last sequence number. One oddity here is that the baseTimestamp\\n71:     field is not preserved during compaction, so it will change if the first record in the batch is compacted away.</p>\\n72: \\n73: ... \n67:     <p>On compaction, we preserve the first and last offset/sequence numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\n68:     producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, for example, then after a partition leader failure, the producer might see an OutOfSequence error. The base sequence number must\n69:     be preserved for duplicate checking (the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer). As a result,\n70:     it is possible to have empty batches in the log when all the records in the batch are cleaned but batch is still retained in order to preserve a producer's last sequence number. One oddity here is that the baseTimestamp\n71:     field is not preserved during compaction, so it will change if the first record in the batch is compacted away.</p>\n72: \n73: ... [chunk truncated]","endLine":75,"startLine":66},{"content":"184:     <p>\n185:     When the group coordinator receives an OffsetCommitRequest, it appends the request to a special <a href=\"#compaction\">compacted</a> Kafka topic named <i>__consumer_offsets</i>.\n186:         The broker sends a successful offset commit response to the consumer only after all the replicas of the offsets topic receive the offsets.\n187:         In case the offsets fail to replicate within a configurable timeout, the offset commit will fail and the consumer may retry the commit after backing off.\n188:         The brokers periodically compact the offsets topic since it only needs to maintain the most recent offset commit per partition.\n189:         The coordinator also caches the offsets Each compactor thread works as follows:\n641:     <ol>\n642:     <li>It chooses the log that has the highest ratio of log head to log tail\n643:     <li>It creates a succinct summary of the last offset for each key in the head of the log\n644:     <li>It recopies the log from beginning to end removing keys which have a later occurrence in the log. __consumer_offsets internal topic and the GroupCoordinator. Here are the key components:\\n\\n### 1. OffsetAndMetadata Storage\\nTwo implementations exist:\\n- **Client-side (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java)**: Contains consumer-facing offset and metadata, with support for leader epoch.\\n- **Coordinator-side (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/OffsetAndMetadata.java)**: Stores server-side offset metadata with commit timestamps and expiration tracking.\\n\\nOffsets are stored in the compacted __consumer_offsets topic as defined in clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/internals/Topic.java, which is used for log compaction to maintain only the latest offset commits.\\n\\n### 2. GroupCoordinator Interface and Implementation\\nThe core coordinator system:\\n- **GroupCoordinator.java** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/): Defines the interface for offset commit, fetch, and delete operations.\\n- **GroupCoordinatorService.java**: Implements the GroupCoordinator interface, orchestrating offset management across multiple coordinator shards.\\n- **GroupCoordinatorShard.java**: Handles offset operations for a specific partition of the group metadata.\\n\\n### 3. Offset Commit Handler\\nThe offset commit flow:\\n1. Client sends OffsetCommitRequest (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetCommitRequest.java)\\n2. KafkaApis.handleOffsetCommitRequest (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaApis.scala) routes to GroupCoordinator.commitOffsets()\\n3. GroupCoordinatorService.commitOffsets() processes the request\\n4. GroupCoordinatorShard.commitOffsets() persists offsets via OffsetMetadataManager\\n5. OffsetAndMetadata objects are stored in __consumer_offsets topic for durability and log compaction\\n\\nThe CommitRequestManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) on the client side manages offset commit requests with retries and batching.\\n\\n### 4. OffsetFetch Request Processor\\nThe offset fetch flow:\\n1. Client sends OffsetFetchRequest (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetFetchRequest.java)\\n2. KafkaApis.handleOffsetFetchRequest routes to GroupCoordinator.fetchOffsets()\\n3. GroupCoordinatorService.fetchOffsets() retrieves stored offsets\\n4. OffsetMetadataManager.fetchOffsets() retrieves from in-memory cache or compacted topic\\n5. Response sent via OffsetFetchResponse\\n\\nThe CommitRequestManager.fetchOffsets() manages client-side offset fetch requests with support for committed offsets lookup.\\n\\n### 5. __consumer_offsets internal topic and the GroupCoordinator. Here are the key components:\\n\\n### 1. OffsetAndMetadata Storage\\nTwo implementations exist:\\n- **Client-side (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java)**: Contains consumer-facing offset and metadata, with support for leader epoch.\\n- **Coordinator-side (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/OffsetAndMetadata.java)**: Stores server-side offset metadata with commit timestamps and expiration tracking.\\n\\nOffsets are stored in the compacted __consumer_offsets topic as defined in clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/internals/Topic.java, which is used for log compaction to maintain only the latest offset commits.\\n\\n### 2. GroupCoordinator Interface and Implementation\\nThe core coordinator system:\\n- **GroupCoordinator.java** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/): Defines the interface for offset commit, fetch, and delete operations.\\n- **GroupCoordinatorService.java**: Implements the GroupCoordinator interface, orchestrating offset management across multiple coordinator shards.\\n- **GroupCoordinatorShard.java**: Handles offset operations for a specific partition of the group metadata.\\n\\n### 3. Offset Commit Handler\\nThe offset commit flow:\\n1. Client sends OffsetCommitRequest (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetCommitRequest.java)\\n2. KafkaApis.handleOffsetCommitRequest (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaApis.scala) routes to GroupCoordinator.commitOffsets()\\n3. GroupCoordinatorService.commitOffsets() processes the request\\n4. GroupCoordinatorShard.commitOffsets() persists offsets via OffsetMetadataManager\\n5. OffsetAndMetadata objects are stored in __consumer_offsets topic for durability and log compaction\\n\\nThe CommitRequestManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java) on the client side manages offset commit requests with retries and batching.\\n\\n### 4. OffsetFetch Request Processor\\nThe offset fetch flow:\\n1. Client sends OffsetFetchRequest (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/requests/OffsetFetchRequest.java)\\n2. KafkaApis.handleOffsetFetchRequest routes to GroupCoordinator.fetchOffsets()\\n3. GroupCoordinatorService.fetchOffsets() retrieves stored offsets\\n4. OffsetMetadataManager.fetchOffsets() retrieves from in-memory cache or compacted topic\\n5. Response sent via OffsetFetchResponse\\n\\nThe CommitRequestManager.fetchOffsets() manages client-side offset fetch requests with support for committed offsets lookup.\\n\\n### 5. Offset Expiry and Compaction Logic\\nOffset expiration is managed through:\\n- **OffsetExpirationCondition.java** and **OffsetExpirationConditionImpl.java**: Define expiration policies based on commit timestamps.\\n- **Group implementations** (ClassicGroup, ConsumerGroup, StreamsGroup) provide offsetExpirationCondition() to determine when offsets should expire.\\n- **OffsetMetadataManager.removeExpiredOffsets()**: Removes expired offsets and produces tombstone records to the __consumer_offsets topic for log compaction.\\n\\nEach group type can customize expiration logic:\\n- ClassicGroup: Uses commit timestamp for expiration\\n- ConsumerGroup: Uses commit timestamp for expiration\\n- StreamsGroup: Uses commit timestamp for expiration\\n- ShareGroup: Does not support offset expiration\\n\\nOffsets are deleted via:\\n- **GroupCoordinator.deleteOffsets()**: Explicit deletion via admin API\\n- **OffsetMetadataManager.deleteOffsets()**: Produces delete tombstones for log compaction\\n\\nThe __consumer_offsets topic uses log compaction cleanup policy to maintain only the latest offset commit per group+topic+partition combination, automatically cleaning up stale offset records.\\n\\n### 6.
